  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3d03421d-11b6-4a65-a975-c7a082ee9d43'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

      $('rating_details').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer15767519652032343036">Jason Dessen is walking home through the chilly Chicago streets one night, looking forward to a quiet evening in front of the fireplace with his wife, Daniela, and their son, Charlie—when his reality shatters.<br/><br/>- - -<br/><br/>'Are you happy in your life?'<br/><br/>Those are the last words Jason Dessen hears before the masked abductor knocks him unconscious. Before he awakes to find himself stra</span>
  <span id="freeText15767519652032343036" style="display:none">Jason Dessen is walking home through the chilly Chicago streets one night, looking forward to a quiet evening in front of the fireplace with his wife, Daniela, and their son, Charlie—when his reality shatters.<br /><br />- - -<br /><br />'Are you happy in your life?'<br /><br />Those are the last words Jason Dessen hears before the masked abductor knocks him unconscious. Before he awakes to find himself strapped to a gurney, surrounded by strangers in hazmat suits. Before the man he's never met smiles down at him and says, 'Welcome back.'<br /><br />In this world he's woken up to, Jason's life is not the one he knows. His wife is not his wife. His son was never born. And Jason is not an ordinary college physics professor, but a celebrated genius who has achieved something remarkable. Something impossible.<br /><br />Is it this world or the other that's the dream?<br /><br />And even if the home he remembers is real, how can Jason possibly make it back to the family he loves? The answers lie in a journey more wondrous and horrifying than anything he could've imagined - one that will force him to confront the darkest parts of himself even as he battles a terrifying, seemingly unbeatable foe.</span>

<a href="/questions/838632-i-really-enjoyed-this-book-but-did-find"><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I really enjoyed this book, but did find myself asking two questions at the end of it. 1) Was it explained how the "boxes" showed up in all the worlds he visited? Did they just appear, and if so, nobody thought that was weird? And 2. Wouldn't there also be an infinite number of his "real worlds" (representing the various things that could've happened since Jason2 took over)? Couldn't each Jason just find a new one? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/998006-loraine"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1595149881i/998006._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/998006-loraine">Loraine</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This was the biggest question I had while reading this! The corridor was a lower-dimensional mental representation of a higher dimension space, allowi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This was the biggest question I had while reading this! The corridor was a lower-dimensional mental representation of a higher dimension space, allowing them access to other worlds. Once in that world, the box should not be there physically. It's not a TARDIS, just a portal of sorts. There is no reason why the box should have manifested and stayed manifested so convieniently in the new world. They would have been dropped into the alternate world and to exit, would've had to build a new box.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1696845377" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1696845377" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1696845377?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=botm">botm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1696845377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1428009402746251200"><blockquote>
  <i>I suppose we’re both just trying to come to terms with how horrifying infinity really is.</i>
</blockquote><br/>This book made me feel tiny. It was overwhelming and scary, but <b>oh so very gripping too</b>. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27833670.Dark_Matter' title='Dark Matter by Blake Crouch' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Matter</a> is the kind of compelling "I must know WTF is going on" book that makes you forget about everything else you had to do that day. You step into this world - this absolute mind fuck of a world that will tug at both your heart strings and your brain cells - and you don't want to come out until you know how i</span>
  <span id="freeText1428009402746251200" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I suppose we’re both just trying to come to terms with how horrifying infinity really is.</i>
</blockquote><br />This book made me feel tiny. It was overwhelming and scary, but <b>oh so very gripping too</b>. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27833670.Dark_Matter" title="Dark Matter by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Matter</a> is the kind of compelling "I must know WTF is going on" book that makes you forget about everything else you had to do that day. You step into this world - this absolute mind fuck of a world that will tug at both your heart strings and your brain cells - and you don't want to come out until you know how it ends. Real life? Who cares? Shit is going down and I need answers!<br /><br />I recently read Crouch's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15034320.Pines__Wayward_Pines___1_" title="Pines (Wayward Pines, #1) by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Pines</a> and was pretty disappointed. It was a great concept, but I thought the TV show was better and I didn't much like any of the characters. That's not a problem here. Jason Dessen goes through some serious shit and it's hard not to find sympathy for him when his life is ripped apart.<br /><br />After being abducted one night by a masked man, Jason is knocked unconscious and wakes in an unfamiliar place, surrounded by unfamiliar people who all seem to think he's somebody he isn't. What happened to him? Where are his beloved wife and son? These are questions that he will try to answer. But, as he discovers more and more about his situation, he starts to doubt what is real and what is not. Doubt whether he'll ever make it back to his life. Doubt whether it ever even existed at all.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I think, like you, like me, like everyone, she had regrets. I think sometimes she woke up in the night wondering if the path she took was the right one.</i>
</blockquote><br />And just when you think you got it. When you think you've wrapped your brain around where this book is taking you and what's going on - well, buckle your seat belts, because this ride is about to get a whole lot crazier. In a good way.<br /><br />It's <b>mind-bending and exciting</b>. I felt connected to the book on a personal level because I shared Jason's horror and the fear that he would never make it back to the family he loves. So it was emotionally engaging. But it was also thought-provoking. I could feel my eyes getting wider as I read further into the story.<br /><br />The sort of "twist" in the plot is the perfect kind. One of those that I really should have seen coming - it was so obvious! - and yet I didn't. At all. So so good.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1700423430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10408379022643601615">I loved the premise of this story.<br/>Are we really happy? What if we made different decisions in life? <br/>What if we could live out choices we never made but wished we did?<br/>What if we went left instead of right?<br/>Straight.<br/>Backward.<br/>Diagon Alley.<br/>Harry Potter.<br/>The premise was very interesting. The stuff about the box and the multiverse and even the science at times was interesting.<br/>Why couldn't you pull that off, Andy Weir?<br/>The plot is so fast-paced and relentless. Even if you aren't fully invested, you want t</span>
  <span id="freeText10408379022643601615" style="display:none">I loved the premise of this story.<br />Are we really happy? What if we made different decisions in life? <br />What if we could live out choices we never made but wished we did?<br />What if we went left instead of right?<br />Straight.<br />Backward.<br />Diagon Alley.<br />Harry Potter.<br />The premise was very interesting. The stuff about the box and the multiverse and even the science at times was interesting.<br />Why couldn't you pull that off, Andy Weir?<br />The plot is so fast-paced and relentless. Even if you aren't fully invested, you want to keep going because it's so easy to keep going.<br />Few paragraphs have more than two sentences. Most have just one.<br />Or just a few words.<br />Or a list.<br />Sausage.<br />Pepperoni.<br />Cheese.<br />Bacon.<br />I use the word "paragraph" loosely.<br />Blake Crouch doesn't use paragraphs at all. Sometimes.<br />Sentences.<br />Words.<br />Little description.<br />All plot.<br />All action.<br />Lots of running. Guns. Murder, kind of. Surprises.<br />Family.<br />Love.<br />Science.<br />It's all there. <br />This book really just wants a few hours of your attention. That's all. It doesn't need you to think too much about it, and it doesn't need you to remember it a few weeks later when you're doing other more important stuff.<br />It just wants to hang out and take you on a little ride for the weekend and then let you off to get back to your real life.<br />Keep your arms and legs inside at all times. Until the ride comes to a complete stop. <br />Thank you for choosing Dark Matter. We know you have choices when it comes to science fiction thriller books, and we thank you for choosing this one to entertain you today.<br />The Martian.<br />Harlan Coben, any of them.<br />No more comparisons.<br />I can see this being made into a movie. Something like The Matrix. Seems like Blake Crouch has all of his stuff turned into TV shows these days.<br />Wayward Pines.<br />Some other show on TNT, I think.<br />I don't know enough to really comment on those.<br />But, I know they're there. <br />They're<br />Their<br />There<br />They're there in their whatever.<br />This is written just like that young adult trilogy, Chaos Walking.<br />The Knife of Never Letting Go is a better book.<br />But, that's just me. I don't even know why I need to say that. They're different books. They're there and they're different books for young adults and their enjoyment there. Yes, they are. They're.<br />Hello there!<br />I do think if we could really do what this book talks about, or if there really is what this book says there is... boy... that would be wild, and I think our heads would explode trying to rationalize it.<br />Boom!<br />Pow!<br />Zap!<br />Zap! only if our heads explode because of a Taser, or a laser beam I guess.<br />Anyway, if you made it this far... I'm sorry. I think you should read this if you want a fun thrill ride one day or two. Don't expect much from Dark Matter and it will get the job done. <br />Zap!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10408379022643601615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781101924471" href="/book/show/27833673-dark-matter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28953843-jennifer-masterson?shelf=audio">audio</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1584841507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18419209988661203439">LOVED IT!!! This book is insanity in a box! 5 stars! Believe the hype! Do not read many reviews! If you like sci fi or want something different and can suspend disbelief read or listen to this book!<br/><br/>This is the audio version review! The audio narrated by actor, Jon Lindstrom, is as good as it gets! He was the perfect narrator for "Dark Matter". This man was born to narrate books! He's that good!<br/><br/>"Dark Matter" starts out pretty simple and then very quickly it turns insane and just keeps getting cra</span>
  <span id="freeText18419209988661203439" style="display:none">LOVED IT!!! This book is insanity in a box! 5 stars! Believe the hype! Do not read many reviews! If you like sci fi or want something different and can suspend disbelief read or listen to this book!<br /><br />This is the audio version review! The audio narrated by actor, Jon Lindstrom, is as good as it gets! He was the perfect narrator for "Dark Matter". This man was born to narrate books! He's that good!<br /><br />"Dark Matter" starts out pretty simple and then very quickly it turns insane and just keeps getting crazier and crazier. When you think it can't get any crazier it does! Trust me! I will never look at a box the same way again! If there is a trigger warning for boxes this book should have it! Lol! <br /><br />Jason Desson is a physicist. He has been married to Daniela for years. He has a son, Charlie, who is almost 15 years old. He's generally a happy guy. He works at a college and loves his family. One day he goes to a bar. When he leaves the bar everything changes! That's it. That's all the plot summery I'm giving you because from there I would be going into spoiler territory.<br /><br />I will share one quote that I think avoids spoilers, but might peak your curiosity: "Is it possible to outthink yourself". Boom! And that's all folks!!!<br /><br />Read it!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18419209988661203439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-story">love-story</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1718843117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12200932355256034060"><blockquote>
  <em>It's terrifying when you consider that every thought we have, every choice we could possibly make, creates a new world.</em>
</blockquote><br/><br/><em>Dark Matter</em>, to be blunt, is miles and miles away from the line that marks my ‘‘comfort zone.’’ I never, or very, very seldom, read books such as this one.<br/><br/>But the truth is, I never read a book like <em>Dark Matter </em>before.<br/><br/>It’s a love story, it’s a thriller, it’s a science fiction book.<br/><br/>It’s thought-provoking, gripping, action-filled.<br/><br/>It makes you think about life and family and wha</span>
  <span id="freeText12200932355256034060" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>It's terrifying when you consider that every thought we have, every choice we could possibly make, creates a new world.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>Dark Matter</em>, to be blunt, is miles and miles away from the line that marks my ‘‘comfort zone.’’ I never, or very, very seldom, read books such as this one.<br /><br />But the truth is, I never read a book like <em>Dark Matter </em>before.<br /><br />It’s a love story, it’s a thriller, it’s a science fiction book.<br /><br />It’s thought-provoking, gripping, action-filled.<br /><br />It makes you think about life and family and what matters most.<br /><br />Who you are, who you were, who you could be.<br /><br />What you want, what you need and what you should have.<br /><br />When to start, when to stop and when to go back.<br /><br />The writing is so very simplistic, but it does the job. It just isn’t the reason why this book is so highly praised. The author manages, however, to bring to life an authentic, loveable and heart-warming hero… or shall I say <em>heroes</em>?<br /><br />There is a lot going on in this story. Don’t you worry, there’s not just action. There’s plenty of inspirational quotes and deep, emotional scenes and surprises.<br /><br />I can’t give this book a five-star rating, because the writing isn’t great exactly and it’s simply not the type of book I would ever reread, but if I were to rate it on my enjoyment alone, my rating would be a four point five.<br /><br />When I said that <em>Dark Matter </em>is thought-provoking, I meant every syllable. There is no way to close this book and not ponder tiny, big things in your life. No way to <em>not </em>question some things or <em>not</em> smile at others.<br /><br />I won’t summarize the story, because I read this having no prior knowledge of what it would contain, and the reading turned out amazing for me. Plus it’s much more poignant this way. You won’t see a thing coming. Even the ending is not what you’ll expect at the beginning. But it’s good. Oh, it’s very good.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12200932355256034060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2008039906?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-sff">adult-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-thriller-mystery">adult-thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2008039906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4100266130586593923"><b>What, with all due respect, the absolute fuck was this book.</b><br/><br/>How do you even start getting over this? How does that happen to someone? I feel very....mmmmm what's the word....confused? lost? so thoroughly <i>mind-fucked</i>? I swear to god my soul has aged for an entire century since I started this book. I wish I could just hollow out a loaf of bread fresh out of the oven and lay in it for a week. Or maybe just sit on top of a mountain, drink some oolong and not think for a month or two. I don't know. M</span>
  <span id="freeText4100266130586593923" style="display:none"><b>What, with all due respect, the absolute fuck was this book.</b><br><br>How do you even start getting over this? How does that happen to someone? I feel very....mmmmm what's the word....confused? lost? so thoroughly <i>mind-fucked</i>? I swear to god my soul has aged for an entire century since I started this book. I wish I could just hollow out a loaf of bread fresh out of the oven and lay in it for a week. Or maybe just sit on top of a mountain, drink some oolong and not think for a month or two. I don't know. Maybe Nasa can fling me into Jupiter to see the inside of that hurricane. I just don't have the energy to be a person right now—this book really wiped me out and I reckon I'll need several days to recover emotionally.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“If there are a million ponds out there, with versions of you and me living similar and different lives, there’s none better than right here, right now. I’m more sure of that than anything in the world.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Here's a summary of Dark Matter:<br><br><b>You are going to be thrown into emotional chaos, lose your mind, and also fuck you lol.</b><br><br>Pretty much.<br><br>This was crazy. Like, mind-fuckingly crazy. I don't even know how to begin to explain it. The only thing I know about this book is that I don’t know anything and I don’t even know if I know that that well.<br><br>Sometimes while I’m reading, I’m like, okay. I got this. My thoughts would start off in one concrete area and I’d have a solid ground to be thinking from. A nice launching pad for a complete thought process. And then—PLOT TWIST. And my thoughts would just take a wrong turn, except instead of a slight detour, I’ll end up in some third lower dimension where I can taste sounds and hear colors or something.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“We all live day to day completely oblivious to the fact that we’re a part of a much larger and stranger reality than we can possibly imagine.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498664083i/23149725._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm really starting to think that everything was better in the early 2000s, especially my ignorance of <b>the multiverse theory</b> and The Lord of The Rings movie.<br><br>Now? Well now that I have read this book, I’m sometimes up during these early night self-destruction hours wondering how many of my alternate universe selves are dead, and thinking about all the parallel universes and different versions of me, and how in one universe I could be a graceful ballet dancer, Iron Man might be my least favorite superhero or I might think One Direction are good or—god forbid—I could hate Cheerios.<br><br>Someone need to collapse the multiverse immediately, I’m going to SCREAM. *drops dramatically to the floor* <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>We’re all just wandering through the tundra of our existence, assigning value to worthlessness, when all that we love and hate, all we believe in and fight for and kill for and die for is as meaningless as images projected onto Plexiglas.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498667649i/23150104._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly though, <b>this book changed me. Like, who am I?</b><br><br>You know those moments when you look in the mirror and you think <i>holy fuck</i>! that’s me! Because for some reason, it feels like the person you’re looking at in the mirror is a total stranger and you begin reflecting on the insignificance and impermanence of life and thinking about how you were miraculously born on one of the few planets out of 100 billion in our galaxy that are capable of supporting life through a delicate balance of heat size and chemical bonding. How you’re just an insignificant blip in a solar system in a galaxy in the infinite structure of the universe...and for a few minutes you seductively slip into existential melancholy?<br><br>I had that moment at 4 am right after finishing this book and I couldn't sleep at all because that mineral that decides whether you sleep… melocotón or whatever…it wouldn’t stop fucking screaming.<br><br>Even worse, I've had to confront a lot of hard truths in my dreams afterwards—my subconscious didn't have to do that and I believe <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/442240.Blake_Crouch" title="Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Blake Crouch</a> owes me so many apologies. Just the other day—and I wish I was making this shit up—I had the most unrealistic and also horrible nightmare and I have never been so happy to be fully conscious and participating in reality; if you must now, it involved an alternate timeline where every single life form is D*nald Tr*mp. *shudders* <br><br>I know this is probably the least informative review of this book that you'll ever read but in my defense, <b>I still have no idea what the fuck I just read.</b> *can't handle it and goes to sleep*</span>
  <a data-text-id="4100266130586593923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1541605515" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1541605515" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1541605515?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1541605515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3493594959894494624">*****NO SPOILERS, I SWEAR.*****<br/><br/><b>”What if all the pieces of belief and memory that comprise who I am--my profession, Daniela, my son--are nothing but a tragic misfiring in that gray matter between my ears? Will I keep fighting to be the man I think I am? Or will I disown him and everything he loves, and step into the skin of the person this world would like for me to be?<br/><br/>And if I have lost my mind, what then?<br/><br/>What if everything I know is wrong?<br/><br/>No. Stop.<br/><br/>I am <i>not</i> losing my mind.”</b><br/><br/>There is nothing more </span>
  <span id="freeText3493594959894494624" style="display:none">*****NO SPOILERS, I SWEAR.*****<br /><br /><b>”What if all the pieces of belief and memory that comprise who I am--my profession, Daniela, my son--are nothing but a tragic misfiring in that gray matter between my ears? Will I keep fighting to be the man I think I am? Or will I disown him and everything he loves, and step into the skin of the person this world would like for me to be?<br /><br />And if I have lost my mind, what then?<br /><br />What if everything I know is wrong?<br /><br />No. Stop.<br /><br />I am <i>not</i> losing my mind.”</b><br /><br />There is nothing more frustrating to a reviewer than reading a book that can’t be written about. Almost every piece of information I could give you about this book is a ***spoiler***. Now, my definition of a spoiler and other people’s definition of a spoiler are not always the same, but in the case of this book the less said, the better. <br /><br />I was very fortunate to watch the movie <i>The Sixth Sense</i> without having a clue about the plot, which is a minor miracle since I’m highly exposed to plots of movies and books, but I was... over the moon... to watch that particular movie without knowing the twist of the plot. So with <i>The Sixth Sense</i> (That plot has nothing to do with this plot, just to be clear.) in mind, I am going to resist the urge to write and write and write about how cool this book is. <br /><br />The first order of business is to convince your friends to read it with you because you are going to want to discuss this book over numerous bottles of wine and a platter of cheese and pretzels. The cheese and pretzels only so you can drink more wine. It would be cruel and unusual punishment to have a designated driver, so my thought is that you should have this book discussion at someone’s house and bring your PJs. Stay over and maybe, if you have the right reasonably attractive friends, you can have….<br /><br /><b>”...fumbling, groping, backset-of-the-car, unprotected because who-gives-a-fuck, protons-smashing-together sex.”</b> <br /><br />So keep that in mind, so that you don’t get <b>TOO DRUNK</b> while discussing this book. <br /><br />Now, anyone familiar with Blake Crouch should know he is a twisty, a twizzler, a zigzagger, a trickster. He bamboozled me in <i>Wayward Pines,</i> and now he has gone even further with Dark Matter. The great thing about this <b>TWIST</b> is that it isn’t just a one off twist...oh no...this is a twist that keeps wrapping itself around other twists until you start to feel little explosions in your head of all those overloaded brain cells. <br /><br /><b>It’s okay, you have plenty to spare. </b><br /><br />By the end of the book and certainly after the protons-smashing-together sex, you will be fully convinced that <i>“...we’re a part of a much larger and stranger reality than we can possibly imagine.”</i> You will also be convinced that you need to read more Blake Crouch books, so you might as well go ahead and factor that into your book budget and *erhhh* food budget right now. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>”What might have been and what<br />has been<br />Point to one end, which is always<br />present.<br />Footfalls echo in the memory<br />Down the passage which we do<br />not take<br />Towards the door we never<br />Opened.<br />--T. S. Eliot, ‘Burnt Norton’”</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I received a free copy of this book from NetGalley and Crown Publishers in exchange for an honest review. <br /><br />If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br />I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3493594959894494624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1624461435" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1624461435" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1624461435?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1624461435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7697219918688267657">Dr. Mr. Crouch,<br/><br/>I was first introduced to your work via my Aunt Janet “The Librarian” years ago; she started me off with your <i>Andrew Z. Thomas/Luther Kite</i> series and I knew I’d found a new favorite author. I branched out on my own and decided to try the <i>Wayward Pines</i> series; somehow I ended up liking that even more than the previous. I was on a roll! Months ago, when I first saw your new book listed on NetGalley, it was vague and sneaky, both things I like in a book, but I decided to wait on requ</span>
  <span id="freeText7697219918688267657" style="display:none">Dr. Mr. Crouch,<br /><br />I was first introduced to your work via my Aunt Janet “The Librarian” years ago; she started me off with your <i>Andrew Z. Thomas/Luther Kite</i> series and I knew I’d found a new favorite author. I branched out on my own and decided to try the <i>Wayward Pines</i> series; somehow I ended up liking that even more than the previous. I was on a roll! Months ago, when I first saw your new book listed on NetGalley, it was vague and sneaky, both things I like in a book, but I decided to wait on requesting until I saw a couple of reviews. Then it hit me-everyone was describing this new book as a love story. A LOVE STORY?! No thanks; not for me. I don’t do that mushy-gushy nonsense. I was disappointed; I had really hoped for something exciting and fresh! As time went on, more of my Goodreads buds kept giving me grief to the point I agreed to read it, but I put it off as long as possible until finally I just needed to clear it off my shelf. I was still a little bitter and possibly throwing a tantrum, but I was going to read it despite your utter betrayal into the land of touchy feely.<br /><br />Boy was I wrong. I know; I should have trusted you. And I finally get all those “this is truly a love story-blah blah blah” comments, because at heart, it is just that. You made sure to include all the intelligent, thrilling components of a Blake Crouch masterpiece that made me almost cancel my date night because I had to read “just one more chapter”. I’m not sure who’s bright idea it was to release your book during this <i>Stranger Things</i> phenomenon, but it was genius. My brain hasn’t had to process this much science since college, and it’s given me the illusion that I can moonlight as an intellectual again. Hehe. Anyway, no plot summary, giveaways, or spoilers here, but thank you good sir for putting in the time and effort to create an unforgettable journey that is sure to stay with all its readers for years to come. I appreciate you keeping it simple enough for my brain to keep up, and hopefully I’m not the only one who feels this way. I’ll be recommending this to everyone in the near future and am sure to include this in my Top Books of 2016 round up.<br /><br />Thanks again, and looking forward to the next book. I promise to be more trusting the next go around.<br /><br />All the best,<br /><br />Chels<br /><br /><b>P.S. I received my digital copy via NetGalley from Crown Publishing in exchange for an honest and fair review. I ended up loving it so much that they sent a paper arc that was leftover and I am eagerly awaiting its arrival to add to my collection of awesome books that were keepers. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7697219918688267657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1725767587" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1725767587" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1725767587?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28684704-dark-matter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=mind-fuck">mind-fuck</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1725767587" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9113737843981451511"><b>Wow. Mind-blown. Amazed. Completely enamored.</b><br/>This book shook me up, made me think and held my heart captive. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461273596ra/18846681.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='“description”/' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I’m beyond impressed with Blake Crouch’s writing. The philosophical nature of this story and his ability to paint such a vivid world with his words really got to me. It shook me to my core. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Are you happy in your life?”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I’m the first to admit, science-fiction isn’t my thing. Not my go-to genre or even one I read with any type of consistency. In fact, it was seeing sci-fi in the blurb t</span>
  <span id="freeText9113737843981451511" style="display:none"><b>Wow. Mind-blown. Amazed. Completely enamored.</b><br>This book shook me up, made me think and held my heart captive. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461273596ra/18846681.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="“description”/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m beyond impressed with Blake Crouch’s writing. The philosophical nature of this story and his ability to paint such a vivid world with his words really got to me. It shook me to my core. <br><br><b>
  <i>“Are you happy in your life?”</i>
</b><br><br>I’m the first to admit, science-fiction isn’t my thing. Not my go-to genre or even one I read with any type of consistency. In fact, it was seeing sci-fi in the blurb that initially made me run the other way. I couldn’t ignore the sheer number of stellar reviews I kept seeing though and ultimately that’s what piqued my curiosity enough to give it a go. I’m so glad I did. <b>I loved every single moment of Jason’s story.</b><br><br>Right out of the gate, it was a heart-pounding, on the edge of my seat, ‘what is going on?’ kind of story. Jason goes from having a quiet family night with his wife and 14 year-old son; to being abducted at gunpoint, stripped naked and taken to an abandoned warehouse. From there, an unexpected journey ensues. It’s a race to find his way back home, to the life he wants and those he loves the most. <br><br>Along the way, the author presents so many questions and quandaries about life. Things that will make you sit back and think. Not only about Jason’s journey, but you might even find yourself examining your own life. If you had the chance to live as a different version of yourself, would you? <b>This book is deep, so be prepared.</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“I can’t help thinking that we’re more than the sum total of our choices, that all the paths we might have taken factor somehow into the math of our identity.”</i>
</b><br><br>Jason was such an easy character to connect with. His sheer will and perseverance is what drew me to him the most. I loved that he never, not for one single moment, wavered on his decision and ultimately what he wanted. <b>What can I say, I’m a sucker for a love story.</b> Which in this instance and in this genre felt completely unexpected, to me.<br><br><b>
  <i>“What would I be without you?”</i>
</b><br><br>My one question - what happened to Amanda? I wish we were given a final chapter from her perspective. I would love to know where she ended up.<br><br><i>*A huge THANK YOU to Crown Publishing and NetGalley for a complimentary copy in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_1676059207" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1676059207" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1676059207?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=we-are-family">we-are-family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=blinded-me-with-science">blinded-me-with-science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1676059207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18442518316807579959">I’m late to the party on this one, and judging by all the 4 and 5 star reviews I can only assume that the mob will be after me with pitchforks and torches for 3 starring it. Come at me, Goodreads!<br/><br/>Jason Dessen is just an average guy with a wife and son he loves, and a job teaching physics at a small college. One night he goes out to meet a friend for drinks, but he ends up being kidnapped by a mysterious man who somehow rips him out of his life and drops him in the middle of a nightmare.<br/><br/>This is o</span>
  <span id="freeText18442518316807579959" style="display:none">I’m late to the party on this one, and judging by all the 4 and 5 star reviews I can only assume that the mob will be after me with pitchforks and torches for 3 starring it. Come at me, Goodreads!<br /><br />Jason Dessen is just an average guy with a wife and son he loves, and a job teaching physics at a small college. One night he goes out to meet a friend for drinks, but he ends up being kidnapped by a mysterious man who somehow rips him out of his life and drops him in the middle of a nightmare.<br /><br />This is one of those books that’s nearly impossible to review without spoilers because so much of what happens comes after major revelations are made. Even if you see the first big twist coming then you’ll probably still be surprised by what comes next. <br /><br />Here’s the 100% spoiler free review: This is an entertaining sci-fi thriller that reminds me of recent books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/866761838" rel="nofollow noopener">Influx</a> (Slightly better than this.) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305286220" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fold</a> (Slightly worse.) It’s got a pretty good hook, and the story is begging to be turned into a movie although the trailer will probably give away the entire plot once they film it. It flirts with big crazy science ideas, but in the end is more interested in being a human drama about family and choices we make. It didn’t hit a mind blowing level for me on the science side, and it did a better than average job for this type of book of getting me invested in the character side. Overall, it still fell a little short of its ambitions.<br /><br />In short, I liked it but didn’t love it. No regrets about reading it, and I’ll see the inevitable movie version if it’s got a decent score on Rotten Tomatoes. <br /><br />To dig into this in more detail here’s some specifics. I’m not giving away the ending, but I do address the overall plot in general terms. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I guessed fairly early on that we were dealing with an alternative universe situation, and that it was another Jason who had kidnapped original Jason so those revelations weren’t shocking to me. However, I was pleasantly surprised when that scope expanded to include the whole multiverse exploration angle, and I thought those ideas were fun.<br /><br />Yet, I was again a little let down that the focus so entirely remained on Jason’s desperate quest to get back to his family, and the guy started to irritate me a bit. He’s seen disastrous consequences as a result of trying to find his wife, and it irked me that as a scientist he never seemed all that interested in any of the amazing things he was right in the middle of. His obsession to get home was incorporated into the story and dealt with in ways I appreciated, but this whole book was constant underlining how the only thing that this character cared about was his family. Which is understandable but felt one-note in a story with the potential to have epic scope.<br /><br />Yes, you could make the argument that was the whole point and that the sci-fi elements were just window dressing for a story about a man literally traveling multiple universes to get back to those he loves. But that runs squarely into a pet peeve of mine. A lot of mainstream fiction peddles the notion that we all have to make a choice between greatness/professional success versus having love/family. Since most of us are just average folks with average jobs but have people we care for in our lives it behooves the creators of these stories to reinforce the idea that we made the right choice, that we’re better off than those who may seem to have it all because we’re told they must surely be lonely and empty without the vital human connections that we have. <br /><br />In short, it’s complete pandering nonsense that I have little patience for anymore. Sure, those who accomplish a lot make sacrifices, but all kinds of people who make their dreams a reality have family, friends, pets, etc. that they care for and spend time with. As an easy example: Follow Lin-Manuel Miranda on Twitter. Then try to tell me that someone can’t have a spouse and child and still write and star in a groundbreaking Broadway play, win a Pulitzer Prize, deal with an insane amount of public attention, get involved in political and social causes, generally make the rest of us look like lazy slack-asses, and apparently have the time of his life while doing all of it.<br /><br />Ultimately I found this to be somewhat unsatisfying because its whole premise is built on that idea. It’s telling that Jason never found a world where his doppelganger had both a successful career and the family. That world would have undercut the central idea that the average Jason, who cares only about his wife and son, was the ‘best’ one. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So its sci-fi elements aren’t as deep or well presented as other books I’ve read dealing with a similar concept, and its major theme rubbed the wrong way a bit. Still, it was an entertaining read with some big ideas that I enjoyed. <br /><br /><i>Note: I'm getting comments that are discussing things I spoiler tagged with no warnings. If you want to comment on some aspect that is under the spoilers section then please use that function. Any comments that don't will be deleted.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18442518316807579959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1676059207">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1893178224" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1893178224" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1893178224?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1893178224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13642421356542966926"><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=f34XzCtirjg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click here</a> to watch a video review of on my BookTube channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/6kLHT7y' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515604004i/24865327._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>To describe this book would be to distract from the elements of surprise, mystery and thrilling confusion found within its pages. <i>Dark Matter</i> is best picked up with as little knowledge of the story as possible and its events explored with the same sense of vulnerable astonishment as the protagonist, Jason Dessen. <br/><br/>The pacing and structure of this novel are brilliant. Events unfold in evermore enticing ways</span>
  <span id="freeText13642421356542966926" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=f34XzCtirjg" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here</a> to watch a video review of on my BookTube channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/6kLHT7y" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515604004i/24865327._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>To describe this book would be to distract from the elements of surprise, mystery and thrilling confusion found within its pages. <i>Dark Matter</i> is best picked up with as little knowledge of the story as possible and its events explored with the same sense of vulnerable astonishment as the protagonist, Jason Dessen. <br><br>The pacing and structure of this novel are brilliant. Events unfold in evermore enticing ways, and Crouch masterfully concludes each chapter in such a way that there's an urgent need to promptly being reading the next one. The unique sentence structure employed by Crouch further increases the sense of speediness and tension. There's no dawdling; everything is immediate. <br><br><i>The warm autumn day is cloudless. <br>Windless. <br>Timeless. <br>The air redolent of - <br>Roasted peanuts. <br>Popcorn. <br>Plastic cups filled to the brim with beer.</i> <br><br><i>The wood is dry and gray, several seasons old, and it quickly takes the flame. <br>Soon the walls of the living room are aglow. <br>Shadows flickering across the ceiling.</i> <br><br>Though complex scientific theories are explored, they are presented in a comprehensive manner that makes them accessible to all readers. One needn't have a degree in physics or mathematics to fully appreciate the phenomena of Jason Dessen's mind-bending venture. <br><br><i>We're all just wandering through the tundra of our existence, assigning value to worthlessness, when all that we love and hate, all we believe in and fight for and kill for and die for is as meaningless as images projected on Plexiglas.</i> <br><br><i>Dark Matter</i> is a sensational technothriller that transcends the ordinary and escorts readers to an unexplored realm of infinite possibility. <br><br><i>I've always known, on a purely intellectual level, that our separateness and isolation are an illusion. We're all made of the same thing - the blown-out pieces of matter formed in the fires of dead stars.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13642421356542966926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1743886957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8868221147770310776">If you liked the film <i>Interstellar</i>, you might like this. I did not like <i>Interstellar</i>.<br/><br/>I found the plot to be intriguing, but not particularly original. It felt like a rehashing of many stories. The themes were pretty much exactly what you'd expect to find in a book about multiple universes: life, love, decisions, fate, acceptance, etc. <br/><br/>And the dialogue was mediocre at best. There were some lines that had me laughing out loud...and they weren't supposed to be funny. "It felt like it was the first </span>
  <span id="freeText8868221147770310776" style="display:none">If you liked the film <i>Interstellar</i>, you might like this. I did not like <i>Interstellar</i>.<br /><br />I found the plot to be intriguing, but not particularly original. It felt like a rehashing of many stories. The themes were pretty much exactly what you'd expect to find in a book about multiple universes: life, love, decisions, fate, acceptance, etc. <br /><br />And the dialogue was mediocre at best. There were some lines that had me laughing out loud...and they weren't supposed to be funny. "It felt like it was the first time you had really seen me. Maybe the first time anyone had ever really seen me. It was the hottest thing." THE HOTTEST THING? Also: "It was like I was something, not that you wanted, but that you needed. Like I was your oxygen." *groan*<br /><br />I hate to be a Debbie Downer, but I really feel like I read a completely different book than everyone else. I just don't get the hype. It's saving grace is that it was a quick read and I never felt like DNFing it. But if it had been any longer I would've definitely skim read the ending only to find out what happens.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8868221147770310776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17704709625442694826">I really like the concept and the hectic trippy-ness that unfurls in the second half of the book, which makes the tail wind of the story a fast and fun ride. The main thing hanging me up is Crouch's cheesy writing. The characters are trite and formulaic, and the protagonist's inner monologue constantly emphasizes the life lesson that Crouch wants you to walk away with. He doesn't leave much room for interpretation or nuance because he keeps slapping you in the face about how life is precious and</span>
  <span id="freeText17704709625442694826" style="display:none">I really like the concept and the hectic trippy-ness that unfurls in the second half of the book, which makes the tail wind of the story a fast and fun ride. The main thing hanging me up is Crouch's cheesy writing. The characters are trite and formulaic, and the protagonist's inner monologue constantly emphasizes the life lesson that Crouch wants you to walk away with. He doesn't leave much room for interpretation or nuance because he keeps slapping you in the face about how life is precious and we shouldn't take things for granted, like some after-school special episode that's peppered with light sci-fi and Diet Coke.</span>

<div id="review_1926972526" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1926972526" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1926972526?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=traveling-friends-read">traveling-friends-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1926972526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2902452945234878266"><b>*4.5 stars!*<br/><br/>Boxes and multiverses and quantum physics, <i>oh my!</i></b><br/><br/>This is one thought-provoking, page-turning, blood-pressure-elevating, fast-paced son of a book, and I enjoyed every little action-packed minute of it!<br/><br/><b><i><blockquote>"The most beautiful thing we can experience is the mysterious."—Einstein</blockquote></i> </b> <br/>I don’t read much science-fiction, and for that reason I’m gonna go ahead and say you don’t have to be a scifi veteran in order to get sucked into the <u>brilliance</u> of this one. You don't even have to be that big a fa</span>
  <span id="freeText2902452945234878266" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 stars!*<br><br>Boxes and multiverses and quantum physics, <i>oh my!</i></b><br><br>This is one thought-provoking, page-turning, blood-pressure-elevating, fast-paced son of a book, and I enjoyed every little action-packed minute of it!<br><br><b><i><blockquote>"The most beautiful thing we can experience is the mysterious."—Einstein</blockquote></i> </b> <br>I don’t read much science-fiction, and for that reason I’m gonna go ahead and say you don’t have to be a scifi veteran in order to get sucked into the <u>brilliance</u> of this one. You don't even have to be that big a fan of the genre, in my opinion. <br><br>It’s best I tiptoe around spoilers here, because *details* can be dangerous little revealers, so I’ll focus on writing…<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"No one tells you it’s all about to change, to be taken away. There’s no proximity alert, no indication that you’re standing on the precipice."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>You know that feeling when you’re reading a book whose ideas are so unique and intelligent and intricately-constructed that you have to reread certain concepts once or five times just to prove to yourself that you <b>got this</b>, and that, no, you are <i>not</i> an actual idiot? <br><br>Well, yeah, some of <i>that</i>, but I sorted it out.<br><br>The way this author has formed a reality based off these concepts is astounding, and all of it—every single minute detail—has a sturdy foundation to stand upon and will hold up well under scrutiny. Go back and check for yourself if you want, Blake’s got it all covered. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Every moment, every breath, contains a choice. But life is imperfect. We make the wrong choices. So we end up living in a state of perpetual regret, and is there anything worse?"</blockquote>
  </i>
</b>(LOVE this quote!)<br><br>The prose here is <b>beautiful</b>—eloquent wording materializing into imagery so vivid you'll feel as though you’re inside of it, leaving your own footprints in the snow alongside these characters. We are made to dissect our choices in life. To be concerned over where they'll lead us and accept the fact that we’ll never truly know unless we live them. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"Until everything topples, we have no idea what we actually have, how precariously and perfectly it all hangs together."</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><b>DARK MATTER</b> is a thrilling ride that'll keep you on edge, tense with anticipation until that final page is swiped. It proposes the theory that we hold the power to create our own reality--our own destiny--an idea not so far off-base for many, myself included, and makes you wonder just how far you’d go to live out your best life possible. <br><br>This story is not only about science, but <b>sacrifice</b> and <b>strength</b> and <b>LOVE</b>. <i>Namely</i> love, in fact—because, truly, what in all the worlds is more important? <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>
</b><br><b>▪  Genre/Category:</b> Science Fiction/Thriller/Mystery<br><b>▪  Characters:</b> Well-constructed and memorable. Not too large a cast.<br><b>▪  Plot:</b> A man of science struggles between world: the one he has, and the one he always thought he’d have.<br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Brilliant. A knock-your-socks-off kind of beautiful prose. <br><b>▪ POV:</b> 1st person Narrative: Hero<br><b>▪  Cliffhanger:</b> None. Standalone<br><br><b>
  <i>*Traveling Friends Read*</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_2317549231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2317549231" />
    <a title="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara"><img alt="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537347712p2/43416866.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2317549231?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgnossia O&#39;Hara" href="/user/show/43416866-evgnossia-o-hara">Evgnossia O&#39;Hara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2317549231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5127659734735505367">Review was originally published on <a href='https://throughthechapters.wordpress.com/2018/03/16/dark-matter-by-blake-crouch-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Through the Chapters|Blog</a><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <p>
    <i>"We all live day to day completely oblivious to the fact that we're a part of a much larger and stranger reality than we can possibly imagine.”</i>
  </p>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I can securely declare that this book have changed the way I perceive the world and my existence in the universe.<br/><br/>But first things first. Dark Matter portraits an ordinary, middle aged professor, Jason Dessen, having a peaceful evening with his wife and his teenage son. After his decis</span>
  <span id="freeText5127659734735505367" style="display:none">Review was originally published on <a href="https://throughthechapters.wordpress.com/2018/03/16/dark-matter-by-blake-crouch-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">Through the Chapters|Blog</a><br><br><blockquote>
  <p>
    <i>"We all live day to day completely oblivious to the fact that we're a part of a much larger and stranger reality than we can possibly imagine.”</i>
  </p>
</blockquote><br><br>I can securely declare that this book have changed the way I perceive the world and my existence in the universe.<br><br>But first things first. Dark Matter portraits an ordinary, middle aged professor, Jason Dessen, having a peaceful evening with his wife and his teenage son. After his decision to meet one of his accomplished friends, who had won a prize on a scientific achievement, his life changes dramatically. During his mind-altering adventure he faces madness, danger, and choices that have to be made. But purely, he receives and realizes that “the Knowledge” of our existence in the universe is both a burden and a blessing that can either improve or destroy our heathen, in so many ways, civilization. <br><br>Our lives consist of simple truths that we accept without doubt. We live on a beautiful planet, we breathe, we fell in love, we make plans about our future, and we are told that we are unique. We rarely contemplate about the universe and the alternative realities that might or might not exist. In any case, are we to blame for our ignorance on topics that are our future? It is the human nature to avoid agonizing about things that are beyond our control. <br><br>But then, you read an article or a book that stimulates you to wonder, to doubt, and to explore ideas and thoughts that are astonishing, intimidating, mind-blowing and insane. And then comes this moment when you think:<br><br><blockquote>
  <p>
    <i>“What if people knew what I know?”</i>
  </p>
</blockquote><br><br>Alternative universes, alternatives realities, a better or worse or a completely deferent version of yourself, and the choices that make you “you”, are the main topics that Blake Crouch is attempting to elaborate in his book “Dark Matter”. I ought to confess that Blake managed to play a severe game with my mind as I’ve got to the point considering about my sanity, after losing myself into the story, the infinite of the universe and the “what if” scenarios. All in all, it was a mind blender.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521223099i/25224670._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Blake pictures a vivid world, which is action-packed, addictive, adventurous, complex and awe-inspiring. His short sentences are like gun shots- this short, this fatal. Using a simple writing-style he “shoots” you with information and a dazzling world where he is the God and the Death himself. <br>He proves that he is a mile away of a pusillanimous writer, by intervening in a field of the multiverse, which seems such a hallucinatory attempt that even some scientists are afraid to consider. <br><br>However, after all, this is the beauty of being a writer. You can write on crazy, overwhelming topics and stimulate the readers to study things that they didn’t imagine they would be interested in.<br><br>Being said that,<br><br><blockquote>
  <p>
    <i>“All your life, you’re told you’re unique. An individual. That no one on the planet is just like you.<br>It’s humanity anthem.<br>But that isn’t for me anymore.”</i>
  </p>
</blockquote><br> <br>It truly isn’t. <br><br>Crouch accomplished to engage me in a way so deep, where I was able to absorb and imagine the unimaginable truths of our existence and made me sing along with “Sleeping At Last” <br><br><blockquote>
  <p>
    <i>
      <b>“How rare and beautiful it truly is that we exist”</b>
    </i>
  </p>
</blockquote><br><br><blockquote>
  <p>I would like to dedicate this review to one of the greatest minds of our days who recently passed away,to <b>Stephen William Hawking</b>. A theoretical physicist, cosmologist, and author, who bequeathed us a great knowledge on the universe and black holes. Stephen Hawking was a vigorous supporter of the many-worlds interpretation and I am convinced that he will continue to be an inspiration for many generations to think outside the box and explore the inexplicable and unimaginable wonders of the universe.</p>
</blockquote><br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/quotes/1510333169p8/363982.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521222795i/25224664._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5127659734735505367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1716417012" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1716417012" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1716417012?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
