        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1716417012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3703826806683853183">Dark Matter is a book that thrills, horrifies and asks deep philosophical questions. It begins with Jason, a physics professor surrounded by his beloved wife, Daniela, and his teenage son, Charlie, cooking supper. He steps out to meet with a long time friend, Ryan, who has been awarded a prestigious prize. On his way home, Jason is abducted, after which life as he knew it shatters.<br/><br/>I found myself seeing the book through the lens of the band, The Talking Heads...their album titles, song titles and</span>
  <span id="freeText3703826806683853183" style="display:none">Dark Matter is a book that thrills, horrifies and asks deep philosophical questions. It begins with Jason, a physics professor surrounded by his beloved wife, Daniela, and his teenage son, Charlie, cooking supper. He steps out to meet with a long time friend, Ryan, who has been awarded a prestigious prize. On his way home, Jason is abducted, after which life as he knew it shatters.<br /><br />I found myself seeing the book through the lens of the band, The Talking Heads...their album titles, song titles and lyrics....this is not my beautiful wife.....Stop Making Sense......Psycho Killer... and so on. Scientific thinking comes into play, the quantum world, string theory and game theory. The mathematics of identity. If this novel was art, it would be a fusion of Surrealism, Cubism and Abstract Art. It is a rumination of all that a person could be, the many paths that could have been followed and decisions taken. <br /><br />Distilled to its essence, this is a story of one man's love for his family. What will he do to get back? Home is the love of Daniela and Charlie. What has to happen to ensure he has a future with them? They are the stars in his sky, they are everything. Wonderful novel. Highly recommended and brilliant read. Thanks to PanMacmillan for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3703826806683853183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/597461-elyse-walters?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710659889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14449642601380904408">I was hooked right away. Exciting -page turner- extremely fast pacing as rumors have spread. <br/><br/>The author has a unique style of writing- very short sentences. "SHOTS OF ADRENALINE"!!!<br/>He also creates clear images from the start -- visuals of family life....[Thurs. night is family night with Jason, Daniela, and their son Charlie]. <br/>The dialogue is intimate - but at times the narration felt laborious - however the author draws us in anyway. <br/><br/>I liked this story... It's almost impossible to put it down -</span>
  <span id="freeText14449642601380904408" style="display:none">I was hooked right away. Exciting -page turner- extremely fast pacing as rumors have spread. <br /><br />The author has a unique style of writing- very short sentences. "SHOTS OF ADRENALINE"!!!<br />He also creates clear images from the start -- visuals of family life....[Thurs. night is family night with Jason, Daniela, and their son Charlie]. <br />The dialogue is intimate - but at times the narration felt laborious - however the author draws us in anyway. <br /><br />I liked this story... It's almost impossible to put it down -as others have said. But I was left with questions - 'why and how' questions. <br /><br />So....FOR PEOPLE WHO 'HAVE' read this book....I have questions: But NO SPOILERS --so if other 'book-lovers' are reading this - my questions won't give anything away.<br />What did you think about Amanda? And am I the only one who wanted to see more developed in her character? Other thoughts about......? [YOU KNOW]<br />Also...did anyone else feel sad for Daniela? I tried to imagine being in her shoes...<br />Daniela was strong and always held her own--almost a saint at times--but I still felt sorry for her. <br /><br />In "Dark Matter", Blake Crouch doesn't just build a world...he explores various incidences of the multiverse. Parts of these worlds were MIND BLOWING-COMPELLING!!! TWISTY THINKING!!<br />Our imaginations are being stretched like an old stretched rubber band. Once over-stretched - there is no way to ever find its way back to its original shape. <br /><br />What makes you you?<br />and <br />What makes me me?<br />ALL YOUR ANSWERS can be found in this novel.....( ha ha), unless you are like me...and come away with QUESTIONS!<br /><br />Either way...this is a groovy train ride! Easy to read in one sitting!!!</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=non-ya">non-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2361202773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14024026026804486975">Ohhhh boy I am daunted by the idea of writing this review.<br/><br/>As many people know, I do a VERY adorable thing where I read a book and then don’t feel like reviewing it straight away so I put it off for a bit and then suddenly it’s been four months and I don’t remember a godforsaken thing about it and I am a shell of the person I used to be when I read the book and the shell of a person isn’t where the book memories are stored!!<br/><br/>Also part of this adorable review-writing process: starting out infinite </span>
  <span id="freeText14024026026804486975" style="display:none">Ohhhh boy I am daunted by the idea of writing this review.<br /><br />As many people know, I do a VERY adorable thing where I read a book and then don’t feel like reviewing it straight away so I put it off for a bit and then suddenly it’s been four months and I don’t remember a godforsaken thing about it and I am a shell of the person I used to be when I read the book and the shell of a person isn’t where the book memories are stored!!<br /><br />Also part of this adorable review-writing process: starting out infinite reviews in the exact same way, delineating the exact same process. Follow for more of the exact same content!<br /><br />Anyway this was a particularly bad time for me to put off writing a review, because I barely understood this book while I was reading it and I sure as sh*t don’t have a comprehensive synopsis to give you now.<br /><br />Basically this book is physics and sci-fi and it’s a little confusing but not in a brain-hurt-y way more like “oh I probably don’t have a full understanding of the causes and/or ramifications of what’s happening here but it doesn’t really matter because I know enough to enjoy this whole plotline situation and I’m not here for a breezy fictionalized physics tutorial anyway.”<br /><br />So if that is what you’re looking for, I can’t really speak on whether you can find it here.<br /><br />What you CAN find is a semi-confusing VERY fun lightly thrilling book that will make you feel kind of smart-ish instead of dumb, like most science-y books! It’s like The Martian, but with more suffering! And also I’m not hungover while reading it!<br /><br />I am also just now recollecting - look guys, progress! - that I had a pretty busy/stressful weekend while I was reading this and I still managed to get it done in the better part of 24 hours. Because this is very gripping on top of everything!!! I should have been very distracted as I had a lot on my mind but guess what, it was all Dark Matter central over here! Kinda. To an extent that is still impressive.<br /><br />I think I should be done now.<br /><br />Bottom line: This is not the type of book I normally read AT ALL and heavens to Betsy am I glad I did. <br /><br />(Note to self: when going outside of comfort zone, preferably do so with reading and not with turns of phrase. That’s how you end up saying sh*t like heavens to Betsy and looking like a goddamn fool.)<br /><br />-------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />well.<br /><br />never have i ever read a book like that before. <br /><br />&amp; it worked out like a dream!!!<br /><br />review to come<br /><br />-------<br /><i>currently reading update</i><br /><br />I DON'T KNOW WHAT'S HAPPENING BUT I'M INTO IT.</span>

<div id="review_3096575353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3096575353" />
    <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn"><img alt="Kevin Kuhn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508679965p2/59568642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3096575353?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin Kuhn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin Kuhn" href="/user/show/59568642-kevin-kuhn">Kevin Kuhn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59568642-kevin-kuhn?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3096575353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3935868041649323652">This is a thrilling plot that I tore through in three days. I must have had a dozen people tell me it was like my novel, so I had to read it. Well, both novels use the ‘many worlds’ theory as a central plot device and both examine the opportunity to relive parts of your life, and both books take place in Chicago, but that’s really where the similarities end. This book is really a very well done, action thriller, mine is much less action, more drama and philosophy. “Dark Matter” reads almost like</span>
  <span id="freeText3935868041649323652" style="display:none">This is a thrilling plot that I tore through in three days. I must have had a dozen people tell me it was like my novel, so I had to read it. Well, both novels use the ‘many worlds’ theory as a central plot device and both examine the opportunity to relive parts of your life, and both books take place in Chicago, but that’s really where the similarities end. This book is really a very well done, action thriller, mine is much less action, more drama and philosophy. “Dark Matter” reads almost like a screenplay and I’m sure it will be an excellent movie. Crouch is a superb writer, clever and bright, and writes action as well as anyone. I really don’t want to discuss the plot much, as that’s one of the strengths of this book, is where Crouch takes the concept of parallel universes/multi-dimensions. It's best to go into this book with a minimal understanding of the plot.<br /><br />I was a little thrown off by his use of short paragraphs. Often, he inserts breaks even when there is no change in scene, idea, or really anything to deserve a paragraph break. Many times, it’s just a series of breaks at every sentence. I don’t think it’s a misunderstanding of the rules, I think it’s an intentional device to create a staccato feel. After I lived with it for a while, it didn’t bother me, and I think it achieved what was intended. Being a speed reader, not much takes me out of the story, and these rapid-fire sentences probably kept me focused on the details more than a traditional approach. <br /><br />As I said, I don’t want to reveal any of the plot, I’ll just say this story moves fast, keeps you guessing, and finishes strong. I enjoyed it all the way though. Five stars! I’m looking forward to the movie and to reading the next novel, “Recursion”.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3935868041649323652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9934992916167022236">Every Labor Day weekend, I travel from my home on the island of Nantucket, to the beautiful State of Maine, for a weekend filled with family, friends and fun. <br/><br/>As exciting as this occasion is, getting there can be a real bitch. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586816476ra/29287655.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It starts with me sitting in my car on a ferry for 2-hours and 15-minutes. Once on the mainland, then comes <u>the drive</u>. <br/><br/>As many of you know, and may have even experienced, Labor Day weekend is one of the busiest travel weekends in the United States. Getting off the Cape and</span>
  <span id="freeText9934992916167022236" style="display:none">Every Labor Day weekend, I travel from my home on the island of Nantucket, to the beautiful State of Maine, for a weekend filled with family, friends and fun. <br><br>As exciting as this occasion is, getting there can be a real bitch. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586816476ra/29287655.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It starts with me sitting in my car on a ferry for 2-hours and 15-minutes. Once on the mainland, then comes <u>the drive</u>. <br><br>As many of you know, and may have even experienced, Labor Day weekend is one of the busiest travel weekends in the United States. Getting off the Cape and through Boston, into New Hampshire and through Southern Maine can be challenging and take a <b>LONG</b> time!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1537544042ra/26333947.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Needless to say, I take great pains to select just the right audiobook for that trip. <br><br>This year, I hit the jackpot! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467676229ra/19616875.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I had heard only good things about this Adult SciFi novel, however, I essentially knew nothing about the plot. Nothing. <br><br>It’s one of those books where people don’t want to spoil anything, so all you are really told is that it is excellent!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1541336138ra/26545666.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Blake Crouch is a bestselling author, who also penned <i>The Wayward Pines trilogy</i>, which was adapted into a well-received television series on FOX starring Matt Dillon. <br><br>I watched it, I enjoyed it, but I never read the books.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566007065ra/28005317.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Dark Matter</i> follows scientist turned Professor, Jason Dessen, as he struggles with the after effects of the strangest night of his life. <br><br>After a couple of drinks at his local watering hole, he is kidnapped and assaulted. When he wakes, and tries to return to his life, nothing is as it should be. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566007065ra/28005318.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book started off with an absolute bang. Crouch wastes no time in getting straight into the action.<br><br>The narrator for the audiobook, Jon Lindstrom, had the perfect voice for this story and it was easy to focus on his storytelling even whilst navigating traffic.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1586816476ra/29287656.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My road trip was essentially a 5-hour drive each way and I was able to complete the book in that time period. <br><br>It was so exciting and confusing, in a good way, that it easily kept me awake and engaged the entire trip. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566007065ra/28005319.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One little thing I will reveal on the plot is that it revolves around a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[multiverse trope <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> which is on of my all-time favorite tropes! <br><br>I was so stoked once I discovered that was where this plot was going. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453009055ra/17771501.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was even more sold than before. I felt it was handled so well as far as the science is concerned and in a very unique fashion. <br><br>Crouch is an excellent writer and I definitely plan to read more of his work!<br><br><i>Dark Matter</i> made my trip bearable. I got where I needed to go and crushed a great book in the interim. Win, win all around. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448542225ra/17157081.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To me, the narrator can make or break a story. <br><br>Even if a book you may enjoy if you were the person reading it, has a terrible narrator, it can completely ruin the story. I would definitely listen to more books narrated by Jon Lindstrom!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

He is married to his long time love, has a teenage son, isn't really rich, his life would be classified more around average. Then I forgot about it, because I'm a mood reader, I think he threatened to cut me several times to get me to read this one. I finally did. Thank you book fairy!</i><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463493066ra/19124408.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I'm highlighting all the weirdos that came from a box in this one. <br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510552848?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelly</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1618705350?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Zoeytron</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498278154?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Ed</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1509786433?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Jan</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1481788473?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Sh3lly</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1568958712?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Vivian</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1511007173?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Eddie</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469447973?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Carol</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498509692?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498662629?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">David</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1471967066?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Mommacat</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1635707731?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathleen</a><br><br>Dang!       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen" href="/user/show/13427823-maureen">Maureen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13427823-maureen?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer3220539602500033720">4.5 Big Fat Stars*<br/><br/>*Thank you to Netgalley and Pan Macmillan for my ARC in exchange for a fair and honest review*<br/><br/>Well - what a ride that was! Not just any old roller coaster ride though (definitely not) but one that was really quite unique. What's this ride about? Well, it's definitely a thrill a minute ride that's for sure, but it's also a love story between Jason & Daniela Dessen, and if that isn't enough, it's mixed with a great big dollop of sci-fi.<br/><br/>The opening scene is one of complete domesti</span>
  <span id="freeText3220539602500033720" style="display:none">4.5 Big Fat Stars*<br /><br />*Thank you to Netgalley and Pan Macmillan for my ARC in exchange for a fair and honest review*<br /><br />Well - what a ride that was! Not just any old roller coaster ride though (definitely not) but one that was really quite unique. What's this ride about? Well, it's definitely a thrill a minute ride that's for sure, but it's also a love story between Jason &amp; Daniela Dessen, and if that isn't enough, it's mixed with a great big dollop of sci-fi.<br /><br />The opening scene is one of complete domesticity, family life at it's most simple and comforting. Jason and Daniela are cooking supper in their brownstone home - their son Charlie quietly doing his homework. But never take things for granted because in just a very short time Jason's life will change for ever. Jason, encouraged by Daniela, decides to walk to his local bar to have a drink with an old buddy, but on his journey home he is abducted at gun point and made to drive to an abandoned warehouse. I won't say any more than this, because it would be too easy to give the whole game away. Just one point though, have you ever wondered which way your life would have gone if you'd decided to take another path, chosen a different option? Well, just be careful what you wish for!<br /><br />In terms of weirdness it doesn't get much weirder than this storyline, but suspend disbelief and just go with the flow, because I think you might find yourself,( along with the rest of us) on the weirdest most exciting roller coaster ride of your life!<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1798506349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1798506349" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1798506349?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781447297567" href="/book/show/31366479-dark-matter">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1798506349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12938464878292291219">Okay, I'm bumping this up to a 5 stars. Even though it's been a few hours since I finished reading it, I genuinely cannot stop thinking about it. This book was bonkers! SO good! Sci-fi was never a genre I gravitated towards, but now I want to read them all!<br/><br/>This book poses the question of “Are you happy in your life?”, after the main character is abducted one night. It's a question the kidnapper poses to him, which leads to them 'swapping lives'. The plot is centred around the initial question po</span>
  <span id="freeText12938464878292291219" style="display:none">Okay, I'm bumping this up to a 5 stars. Even though it's been a few hours since I finished reading it, I genuinely cannot stop thinking about it. This book was bonkers! SO good! Sci-fi was never a genre I gravitated towards, but now I want to read them all!<br /><br />This book poses the question of “Are you happy in your life?”, after the main character is abducted one night. It's a question the kidnapper poses to him, which leads to them 'swapping lives'. The plot is centred around the initial question posed and takes off from there. It's definitely best to go into it knowing as little as possible. <br /><br />The concept and approach of the storyline was just ingenious. It completely blurs the line of what's real, or what we perceive to be the reality that has been fixed and known to the world for eons, and the possibility that there are 'other worlds' out there, other versions of ourselves, living the life that we perhaps intended or that steered in a direction we weren't anticipating. For a thriller novel, it's quite philosophical and I love that, calling the readers into question, making it engaging and to decipher what we want from this life and what's important to us. <br /><br />It was exciting, exhilarating and extremely thought-provoking. Since I highly doubt we'll be experiencing the journey this character went on, it was still extremely engaging. You pause. Have a moment. Think about the choices you've made in your life. You're taken on a whirlwind that doesn't stop and keeps on getting crazier. Has you gaping. Mouth open. WTF. Deceives you into thinking that things will start getting back to normal again, till the author decides to surprise you and mess with your mind again. And on it goes. <br /><br />Highly recommend it if the concept sounds interesting to you. Even if you're not into sci-fi, this will probably make you love it. Or at least spark a huge interest.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12938464878292291219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1826969785" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1826969785" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1826969785?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1826969785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14231746829402760244">A steaming hot cup of whatthef***???<br/><br/>Like Crouch’s 2012 mega hit <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15034320.Pines__Wayward_Pines___1_' title='Pines (Wayward Pines, #1) by Blake Crouch' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pines</a>, it’s hard to say much without fatal spoilers, but trust me and 90% of the readers who’ve read and enjoyed this – it’s a wild ride.<br/><br/>Scientist and professor Jason Dessen is abducted in a back alley in Chicago and his life is changed irrevocably. Crouch explores the concepts of the multiverse and also about identity, relationships, and existentialism.<br/><br/>I read a Heinlein short story years ago (and have forgotten the title) where peo</span>
  <span id="freeText14231746829402760244" style="display:none">A steaming hot cup of whatthef***???<br><br>Like Crouch’s 2012 mega hit <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15034320.Pines__Wayward_Pines___1_" title="Pines (Wayward Pines, #1) by Blake Crouch" rel="nofollow noopener">Pines</a>, it’s hard to say much without fatal spoilers, but trust me and 90% of the readers who’ve read and enjoyed this – it’s a wild ride.<br><br>Scientist and professor Jason Dessen is abducted in a back alley in Chicago and his life is changed irrevocably. Crouch explores the concepts of the multiverse and also about identity, relationships, and existentialism.<br><br>I read a Heinlein short story years ago (and have forgotten the title) where people could choose to live on a seemingly infinite collection of worlds, each connected to the “real” world but all different, from subtle nuances to wildly and dangerously dissimilar. This is also vaguely reminiscent of Poul Anderson’s 1965 novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/890300.The_Corridors_of_Time" title="The Corridors of Time by Poul Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Corridors of Time</a>, though Crouch steers clear of outright time travel. And that’s a good thing because if he added time travel to the mix, our heads would explode.<br><br>It started weird, got weirder and then Crouch tapped the nitro button and fishtailed ludicrous speed into REALLY WEIRD.<br><br>Fans will also see influences from Philip K. Dick and the 1999 Spike Jonze film Being John Malkovich came to mind.<br><br>I see that film rights have already been sold and Crouch is working on the screenplay. It should be a cool movie.<br><br>Recommended.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567598594i/28097937._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14231746829402760244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('URekmt0iZ6YLigEaxoyWTcEiPeWsRdY5dxHcETyLxRLmQX/U6gq8TRxmyOrAQT75rXIQUzLCyMLLSLrdpfYzNQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gLpwHoLNMz48FKxb5f01k31cTaJB+m3Ml/9rLWpfSMA37KtQteXo1Sv4ZavjMJ0nEQxgFN99czcrpg3h8yK+5w==')})
  }

But it seems like too good an opportunity to miss—a live-in nannying post, with a staggeringly generous salary. And when Rowan Caine arrives at Heatherbrae House, she is smitten—by the luxurious “smart” home fitted out with all modern conveniences, by the beautiful Scottish Highlands, and by this picture-perfect family. What she doesn’t know is that she’s stepping into a nightmare—one that will end with a child dead and herself in prison awaiting trial for murder. Writing to her lawyer from prison, she struggles to explain the unravelling events that led to her incarceration. It wasn’t just the constant surveillance from the cameras installed around the house, or the malfunctioning technology that woke the household with booming music, or turned the lights off at the worst possible time. It wasn’t just the girls, who turned out to be a far cry from the immaculately behaved model children she met at her interview. It wasn’t even the way she was left alone for weeks at a time, with no adults around apart from the enigmatic handyman, Jack Grant. It was everything. She knows she’s made mistakes. She admits that she lied to obtain the post, and that her behavior toward the children wasn’t always ideal. She’s not innocent, by any means. But, she maintains, she’s not guilty—at least not of murder. Which means someone else is. Full of spellbinding menace and told in Ruth Ware’s signature suspenseful style, The Turn of the Key is an unputdownable thriller from the Agatha Christie of our time.<\/span>\n  <a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3155957814295523473">Blake Crouch is a bestselling novelist and screenwriter. He is the author of the forthcoming novel, Dark Matter, for which he is writing the screenplay for Sony Pictures. His international-bestselling Wayward Pines trilogy was adapted into a television series for FOX, executive produced by M. Night Shyamalan, that was Summer 2015’s #1 show. With Chad Hodge, Crouch also created Good Behavior, the T</span>
  <span id="freeText3155957814295523473" style="display:none">Blake Crouch is a bestselling novelist and screenwriter. He is the author of the forthcoming novel, Dark Matter, for which he is writing the screenplay for Sony Pictures. His international-bestselling Wayward Pines trilogy was adapted into a television series for FOX, executive produced by M. Night Shyamalan, that was Summer 2015’s #1 show. With Chad Hodge, Crouch also created Good Behavior, the TNT television show starring Michelle Dockery based on his Letty Dobesh novellas. He has written more than a dozen novels that have been translated into over thirty languages and his short fiction has appeared in numerous publications including Ellery Queen and Alfred Hitchcock Mystery Magazine. Crouch lives in Colorado with his family.</span>
